Therefore, my sons, since I have committed this book to you, which is the last in the science of medicine, by its completion it shall be completed through you, and by its explanations, and by its declarations, it is evident to me that I commit this treatise on surgery to you.
Since surgery is almost completely abandoned in our region and in our times, it is greatly endangered by peril, and the science of it is lost; there remains only a few small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which are misunderstood and lead to error and confusion before their intentions and power are understood and their art is extended.
It appears to me that I will organize this treatise in the second way, through explanation and declaration and abbreviation; and because it comes with the shapes of the cautery tools and other instruments of the work, along with the addition of the declaration, and the preparation of them, which is necessary.
However, the reason that a good craftsman is not found with his skill in our times, is because the art of medicine is long and requires its practitioner to be exercised in the science of anatomy, which includes understanding the joints and forms of the members; knowing the connection and separation of them; having knowledge of bones, nerves and ligaments, their number, and their function; and the origin of blood vessels, quiet vessels, and pulsating ones; and the location of their emergence.
And as Hippocrates said, "A name is nothing, but in the work it is much, and especially in the art of the hand."
However, we have already said this in the introduction of this book; because whoever is not acquainted with what we have said about anatomy, is not fit to avoid error and risk causing death for men, as I have seen many times, because some are uneducated in this science and abandon it without its knowledge and experience.
Because I saw a foolish and experienced doctor make an abscess called scrophulus on the neck of a woman, and he cut some arteries in her neck, causing a large amount of blood to flow, which resulted in the woman dying among others.
And I saw another doctor who took out a stone from a man's body that had been suffering from the disease for some time, and the stone was large; he came to him and removed the stone with a piece of the bladder, causing the man to die on the third day.
And I myself called for it to be opened, and I saw that due to the size of the stone and the condition of the patient, it was clear that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who took payment from a duke of our land for surgery, and he treated a blacksmith who had a fracture in his thigh; and the doctor prepared himself with his ignorance, cut open the fracture with pulvines and pins with strong construction, but did not let the wound breathe.
Approach the wound according to their wishes, and close it, and let it dry for several days and command that we unbind it; and this way it will be until the flesh and limb are healed, and it may lead to destruction.
Then you should be called to it, and prepared to undo the bandage, and wait for peace and let him endure his pain.
But corruption was already confirmed in the member, so it could not be stopped, and the corruption spread through the member until the patient is in danger.
And another doctor found an abscess cancerous, and it became ulcerated near some days, until the evilness of it was magnified by its lord.
The cause is that the cancerous tumor is full of melancholic humor, so it may not spread to everything, but only to an area that suffers from it all.
And for this reason, my sons, it is necessary that the operation be divided into two divisions: one is the operation associated with health, and another is the work in which there is the greatest risk of danger.
And you have already experienced this in all places of this book in which there is an operation in which there is error and fear; therefore, it is necessary for you to guard against this and let go of it, so that the fools do not take a wrong path and dishonor you.
And therefore, take up your weapons with solicitude and with the protection of God, and your patients with happiness and firmness.
Take the best path for God's grace to lose and attain salvation and laudable succession, and leave behind the terrible illnesses of difficult healing, and withdraw your weapons from what terrifies you, so that examination in your faith and in your name does not mislead you: for more remains for your glory, and thus also in this world and forever to your sanctity.
Gaulia then said in some of her monasteries: "Do not treat evil illnesses, so that bad doctors are not named".
And I have already divided this book into three chapters.
The division of the book begins, and it starts with the first section of the first division. The first chapter ordered for the foot, in the forms of instruments and in the ironwork of the cauteries, and about what is necessary in the operation.
The division of the second division. The second chapter, of cysts and perforations, and of abscesses, and of plagues, and of extraction of sacs and similar to those, all in one chapter and ordered according to the forms of instruments.
The third chapter is ordered for the restoration and dislocation, and cure of twists and similar to those; the chapter is divided into the foot, and forms of instruments.
It is necessary that I say the quality of the benefits and harms of this cautery, and in what kind of circumstances cautery should be prohibited.
So I will say that the discussion of the benefit of cautery and its harm is a long, intricate, and subtle discourse, and secretly hidden; and many wise people have spoken about it, and they have disagreed with each other, and my words are among the few of theirs, fearing tediousness.
And therefore I say that cautery applies universally to all matter or substances, except for two cases, which are cases of caution without substance.
In the case of dry and desiccated matter with substance, there is disagreement; for some say that cautery is beneficial in this case, while others say the opposite, that cautery is not appropriate for illnesses of quality and desiccation, because the nature of fire is of quality and desiccation, and it is appropriate that dry and desiccated matter that is cauterized should be healed.
And I say the opposite of that, that cautery is beneficial in all dry and desiccated illnesses that come into the bodies of men, because when you compare the body of a man and the humidity in it to the nature of fire, you find that the body of a man is extinguished by fire.
And I say through the discussion of this, that I have experienced this myself on several occasions.
But it is not necessary that this comes to the one who has already been explained and practiced in the chapter of cautery in a previous exercise, and has come to know the diversity of the cases of men and the disposition of illnesses in their bodies, and the causes of these, and the accidents of them, and the time span of those.
But in other cases, there is no fear for you, and especially in cold and wet illnesses, because all doctors have agreed on these, and there is no disagreement about the benefit of cautery in those.
Understand, sons, that the secret of healing by cautery with fire and the goodness of it is above cautery as medicine burns, is because the fire is simple, its action does not extend to the member being cauterized except for minor harm to the adjacent member.
But the action of burning medicine spreads to the member adjacent to it, and strong heat brings the disease in the ill member to worsen and accelerate.
But fire, by its sublimity and the goodness of its substance, does not accomplish this; it is already known to us through experiment and the long duration of study on the art concerning the truth of causes; and because it is not lawful for me to reveal my secret hidden in the fire, and the quality of the operation of it in the body and its expulsion of diseases, philosophical demonstrative speech, which could sharpen your thoughts, I shall abstain.
Understand, sons, that they disagree about the time when it is appropriate to perform cautery and pause in the best time of springtime.
I say that cautery is appropriate in all times, because the harm caused by an accidental time is submerged in the benefit of what the cauterization achieves, and especially if the cauterization is for pains or necessary pains, fistulas, which cannot tolerate delay, it is feared that the evil of those who come with malice, which is greater than minor harm entering through the time.
And do not think in your thoughts, or sons, that this is not believed only by the common people and foolish doctors, because the remedy of that illness which is cured with cauterization does not work at all times, and they pause due to its consequences.
And the cause is not as they think, because cauterization is not simply a medicine that alters the complexion and dries the moisture which is the cause of the pain.
But nevertheless, cauterization exceeds medicine by the desire for its value and virtue of its operation and the greatness of its Lord.
It is possible that the illness may return at some hour of time, according to the complexion of the patient and the location of their illness, and the virtue of it, and what is prepared in the body of them due to the accumulation of superfluidities in them, and what is obtained for them through their diet and similar things; but that the illness in which cauterization is administered is a subtle illness in a member with few superfluidities and moisture, such as cauterization of teeth for pain, it is possible that the pain will not return there, but only something small may occur.
But the common saying is that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, and this is not the right one, as I understand it, because I believe that it is not healing which benefits from medicine or any other reason for caution.
And the cause is in opposition to this; and I understand that the saying "cauterization is the last resort of medicine" is not because we administer the methods of healing for some illnesses, and those medicines do not confer improvement, but rather when the end of the illness has been reached, cauterization is administered and improves it. And from here onwards, understand that cauterization is not the last resort of medicine, not according to the meaning which I understand by the common people and the flocks of foolish doctors.
The ancients said that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron, and they did not say this only because of the equality of gold and its sublimity of substance.
And they said that the location of cauterization does not make any difference, because this is not absolutely true, as I already have proven and discovered that it does not do anything except in some bodies, and cauterization with gold is better than with iron as they said; but when you perform cauterization with fire and gold, it is not declared to you, because it depends on the amount of gold that you want according to its cost, and it prepares to receive friction; if you place it on fire some layers so that the artificer can work with it.
And because of this, cauterization with iron must be done more gently and more carefully in the operation.
And I have organized this chapter on cauterization according to the chapters, and I have ordered those of the head within the feet, so that I alleviate the demand for it.
The first chapter.
This cauterization is for the coldness and moisture in the head, which is the cause of the swelling and multiple abscesses called corissa, from the forehead to the hairline and flowing ears, and multiple sleeping, and toothache and headaches, and generally of all illness that comes from coldness, such as paralysis, sodium, apoplexy, and similar ones in those illnesses.
The form of this cauterization is as follows: first, you command the patient to be evacuated with a purgative medicine cleansing the head for three or four nights, according to the strength of the illness and the age and habits of them.
Approach and command him to shave his head with a razor, and then have him sit on a chair and place his hands on his feet.
Then pause your hand at the base of your palm above the nose between your eyebrows. However, when the place you mentioned is reached, mark it with a probe, and then ignite the olive oil cautery which has this shape:
Then place it on the marked spot and press down gently so that it descends, while your hand should be gently tightened around it, and you rotate it.
Then lift your hand slightly and look at the spot, if you see any part of the bone exposed, as with grains of sand, raise your hand again, and if it does not turn back, use another tool, if it is frozen, until the bone that I told you about is visible.
Then take some salt and dissolve it on the spot and leave it for three days.
Then place it over the burned area in bandages and leave it until the scar from the fire is destroyed. Then treat the location with a strong four-part medicine until it is healed.
It has been said that when the wound remains open, the best thing to do is to apply honey, as it is better and more helpful.
Some have said that the vertebra should be cauterized to the bone, and the cautery should be held in place until a piece of the spinal cord is burnt off.
Then scrape away the part that is touching the bone and treat it.
Some have said that when the cautery reaches the nerve, it should be pressed into the bone forcefully until the bone cracks, and this is the shape of the probe: They believe that the vapors from the head will exit from that spot.
The wound should be kept open for a long time and treated until it is consolidated.
However, in my opinion, these two types of cautery are not beneficial to everyone, but only to certain individuals out of fear; and you should discard it, because it is better for the patient's health when possible, as the head is more susceptible to damage from prolonged heat due to its constant exposure, especially if the patient has a frail constitution.
The first type of cautery is safer and better in my opinion; and from that point on, avoid this procedure for the sake of the patient's health.
Chapter two.
On head cauterization.
When chronic and prolonged pain occurs in the entire head of a patient, and it is treated with lancets, hooks, capirushers, ointments, plasters, guaze, needles, blisters, and similar remedies, especially if cauterization has already been attempted but did not improve the situation, then consider whether the patient's head is naturally strong or frail; if it is strong, do not hesitate to cauterize again with a different cautery tool. Approach the cautery to that spot on his head and use it until the scalp is divided. Measure the amount that has been calculated and make an incision in the scalp to expose the bone at that location, which is called the "foramen" - this is the location where a ventous vein is usually found. Then use a cautery to burn and seal off the wound on the back of the head where the incision was made. Then release your hand from there, and do not expose the bone, as the patient will experience a great pain different from the pain caused by other head cauterizations.
Tell the assistant to place this cautery in its location, as the cautery used for burning the corners and top of the head is more subtle than the one used for other locations on the head; this is the correct way to do it.
Title: Tightening
Treatise on Modern Migration Cauterization
When there is persistent pain in the scalp or spreading pain into the neck, medications that modify the head should be administered along with other treatments as I have described in the treatment of diseases; if this does not help, then cauterization should be done in two ways: either cauterization with acute burning medicine, or with iron.
Take a salve of alum, scour it and remove the edges of both sides with a knife. Approach the location of the pain on the temple with a thin lancet and make an incision until it penetrates deeply enough to create a small cavity, but ensure that it remains hidden.
Place a piece of damp cloth over the area with strong compression and leave it for three hours; then remove the alum, let the wound heal for two or three days, and place a plaster over the moistened area until the spot turns black.
Cure that which is inflamed until it heals.
And if you wish, do this with some burning medications that I have written about in the second treatise on burning medications.
Cauterization with iron can be done in this manner: fire for the cauterizing tool, and here is the method for that.
It is called claus clavilhs (key nails), as the tip of it is shaped like a clove with some curvature, and in its middle part there is a small elevation.
Place your hand over the location of the pain, and hold it there - to prevent the archery that is about to come from being disturbed - and rotate the small iron tool slowly.
If the quantity that is pressed by the scalp in this manner is too large and causes bleeding, raise your hand to ensure that the artery, which is nearby, is not pressed, preventing blood flow.
Approach a wound with salt water and cover it over the area, leave it for three days; then approach with a linen cloth stitched, and treat it with oil until it is healed.
If you wish, cauterize the end of the swordsmith's finger according to the cautery, and be careful not to cut an artery during this modern procedure.
Fourth Chapter.
Title: Ancient Cauterization of Hernia.
When treating a hernia with the remedy you have mentioned in the previous cure and in the section on diseases, and if that treatment does not help, and sometimes because of the illness that does not respond to the remedy you have mentioned for the first cautery or the cauterization with fire, then it is necessary that you heat the cauterizing iron until it becomes white-hot, because this signifies the spot of pain marked with a line of appropriate size, and if that cannot be done, hold it for a moment and then pierce the artery and reach the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to be careful about the continuation of the jaw, which must remain healthy for chewing, and that the ligament is not adhered and the nerves that are near it, and that no spasm occurs.
And if it is about the care and caution of blood flow from the artery that is cut off, because in the cutting off of it there is fear, especially for those who do not know what they are doing and are not careful or experienced; leave the operation for a while at the beginning.
And you will find the regulations for dealing with blood flow from an accident of the artery according to its method, in its place in this book.
If you see this illness that does not respond to the cautery and if you find the body of the patient tolerable, cauterize it in the middle of the head as we have recorded, and heal the wound until it is healed.
If you wish, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on arterial constriction with cauterization using two knives, and this cauterization is more effective and appropriate.
Fifth Chapter.
Title: Cauterization of Earaches.
When there is pain in the ear due to cold and it is cured by medicinal causes or other treatments as mentioned in the section on diseases, but the pain persists, then burn the cautery, which is called a point, and this is its form:
Approach the point towards the burning, and place it around the entire ear as a wheel is rolled, or in the circle of each example if the pain is in each one. With the cautery of the ear lance slowly, little by little, because you will feel the place where to stop.
If the cautery of many points is performed on the entire ear, and this is done, then heal the areas until they are healed.
Sixth Chapter.
Title: Cauterization of Torture.
Torture which is cured and treated with cauterization is nothing but the species that come from the plague, as we have mentioned in the section on diseases.
Avoid cauterization of the species that enter by dryness or spasm of the nerve.
When treating that species of torture with jars, poultices and liniments, and if your treatment does not work, then it is necessary for you to cauterize the patient with three cauterizations: the first one is the lancing of the ear, the second a small one at its temple, and the third the junction of two lips.
Pause your cautery on the contrary side of the affected area, because softening does not occur except in the affected part that appears healthy.
The method of cauterization is to cauterize it on the right side of the affected area, placing a small piece of charcoal on top of its head and another on its temple, the length of which should be according to the length of the finger used, and stop your hand with the cautery until the amount of the substance of the burn has been burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, it belongs to the blacksmith, its shape is like a table. However, it is very delicate, and care must be taken to avoid excessive roughness in it; cut the knife thinly in it.
And take care of the area until it has healed.
Chapter VII.
On the ancient method of cauterization for apoplexy.
When apoplexy is old and the patient's condition is stable and they do not have a fever, then cauterize it with four cauteries: above all on the corners of their head; also on the forehead and the sides of the head as described before; and on the neck. The method of cauterization is as previously described.
It has already been cauterized on the stomach opening, and it is later; take care of it as prescribed by the doctor.
Chapter VIII.
On the method of cauterization for forgetfulness caused by a blow.
Give the patient large and round pills in the beginning, as they will soften them.
And shave the entire head of the patient and stop at the neck, applying the plaster described in the treatise on plasters.
Wait for several days, because this is the method of cauterization. Do as the doctor orders, which has already been mentioned.
And if the patient recovers well in this manner, then stop the treatment; otherwise, perform three cauterizations on the lower part of their head, starting from the highest point on their head and moving down towards the neck. Wait between each cauterization for the duration of the finger used, and take care of the cautery as prescribed.
However, if you wish to increase the treatment and the patient is tolerant of it, cauterize in the middle part; otherwise, cauterize on both corners.
Take care of the treated area until it is healed; make sure that the olive oil-based cauteries are as described earlier.
Chapter IX.
On the method of cauterization for relief and softening of the entire body.
You should perform the softening treatment on the patient's head with jars and as previously described; shave the head of the patient, cauterize in the middle part of their head with a cautery, cauterize around all the corners of the head, cauterize at the base of the neck, and apply three cauterizations to the cervical vertebrae.
If it is necessary for the treatment of severe softening of the body and the patient can tolerate it, then cauterize the affected area with four cauteries on the lumbar vertebrae, and then cauterize again until the burn has penetrated deeply, and raise the hand. And apply care to that which is to be healed, and this should be olive oil cauterization.
In the tenth chapter, it is written:
On the Cauterization of Epilepsy
The epilepsy is not cauterized but rather that epilepsy caused by phlegm.
Therefore, it is necessary to treat the brain of the patient at the beginning with oil and with the other treatment which has been said in the division when the patient is strong and tolerates the exception of medications.
If the patient is a child who does not tolerate medications, then administer gruel and gruel-like foods that are easy to digest, with the intention of improving their diet for several days.
Then shave the head of the patient, then cauterize that area with a cautery in the middle of the head according to the method previously mentioned, and another cautery on the occiput of the patient, and over each ear cauterize as well. If the patient is strong and tolerates it, then cauterize that area with the cauteries which have been mentioned, achieving paralysis and softening of the body on the vertebrae in the neck and the vertebrae in the back.
And use olive oil cauterization as previously mentioned.
But if the patient is a child, then pause with a subtle cautery according to this method.
In the eleventh chapter, it is written:
On the Cauterization of Melancholy
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize that area with the cauteries which have been mentioned for achieving paralysis.
If the cause of melancholy is excess declining into melancholy and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink that cleanses the brain as has been previously mentioned in the division.
Then shave the head of the patient, then make an incision in a circle around it, and then pause that incision in the middle of the head.
The patient should be held securely on all sides.
Then pause with a lint dressing; it is also appropriate for use as an old sheep's balm. Heat that area over the fire at a suitable temperature, which the patient will tolerate when it is applied to them. Then apply that over the middle of the head in a circle and leave it in place until it is soaked through.
Give that to the patient every week once, with the other treatment for their good health until they are healed; or if you wish, cauterize that area making small points as much as possible, but always have a well-ordered cautery at hand: this is the specialty of cauteries which moisten the brain equally.
Then pause that area in a cloth or bandage made of woolen thread.
In the twelfth chapter, it is written:
On the Cauterization of Water Dropping into the Ear
When you have recognized the onset of water in the ear through the signs which I mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something to drink that cleanses their head, and keep them away from all moisture.
Let them bathe in warm water for several days.
Then tell them to rinse their head and cauterize that area with a cautery in the middle of the head; then cauterize that area with two cauteries on each temple if it is the onset of water in both ears, or one cautery if it is the onset of water in one ear.
Make incisions with a cautery on all veins and arteries that have already been tied off; let the cauteries be in a line at the level of the temples.
Be careful of blood flow when cauterizing; and if you see blood flowing from it, apply some medicine to stop the flow, which is within your ability.

Chapter XVI.
On the eyelid cautery when the hair is transformed into parts inside and pierce the eye.
When the eyelid hair is transformed into parts inside and pierces the eye, cauterize them in two ways, for there are two types of cautery: one to burn or one to use medicine to cauterize.
If the cautery is to burn, tell the patient to pull out their eyelashes as when they pluck them, but extend and curl them; if you pierce it (the eye), then you must cleanse its wound, and then cover the eyelids with a bandage until the hair grows back.
So when the eyelashes grow and curl back, place a cloth on the patient's head and apply pressure to the eyelid of the eye with the thumb, following the shape of a holly leaf, and start the pressure near the hair.
Then place cotton soaked in hog's fat or chicken oil on the eye.
And bring fire to the shape of the cautery.
And cauterize on the shape that was marked, little by little, in small spots, until the surface of the skin resembling holly leaf is burned completely and appears properly.
The sign of the cure of this operation is that you see the eyelid of the eye contracted and the hair on it raised due to the piercing of the eye.
And so lift your hand and let it rest there for three days, and then cover the cotton with a bandage until the scar has healed. And cure that (eye) with eye drops until it is healed.
But if the hair returns for some reason and the eyelid is softened again, then perform the cauterization once more in the same manner as you did initially.
But if the hair is in the eyelid, then cauterize it so that it is raised to its natural position, curl up and that it does not pierce the eye.
But the cautery with medicine to burn is that you tell the patient to pull out their eyelashes until they grow and curl back, and make a paper of cloth in the shape of a holly leaf.
And take a known powder and fresh live juice (of some plant). that is, The text advises to mix the known powder and fresh juice (of some plant) with haste so that it is not spoiled; spread it over the cloth shaped like a holly leaf and apply it to one or both eyelids, and cover the affected eye with cotton soaked in hog's fat. The patient's head should be on your lap.
The text mentions that the patient should rest the affected area on the medication and press it gently without causing discomfort until the patient feels the sensation of the medicine, which is similar to being burned. In medieval medicine, this could be understood as allowing the medication to take effect and work its healing properties on the affected area. The comparison to a burn suggests that the medication may cause some degree of discomfort or pain, but it is tolerable for the patient.
And when the patient perceives the sensation of the medicine, they should remove it and rinse their eye with water. Then consider if the eyelid has been raised as it should be, either by burning or incision (surgery). If so, then the operation is successful; if not, apply more medication on the unaffected area without pressing too hard and allow the healing process to continue until the eyelid is raised.
The text advises to cover the affected area with cotton and bandage until the scar from the burn or incision heals. Then cure it with eye drops or another method until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you, you must keep your operation under vigilant diligence so that no remedy falls into the eye, and if the eyelid becomes swollen for some days due to the skin's inflammation in the eye, then apply your medicine on that location where the eyelid is swollen. And do as before, and return until it is healed.
Here is the form of mistletoe.
You should know that men's eyes vary in size and amount, so accordingly you make your treatment.
It shall not be hidden from the one who studies this art.
Chapter XVII.
On cauterization of fistula that is in the tear duct of the eye.
When you treat fistula as I have said in the division of diseases and do not confer your treatment, then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this method: command the patient to hold their head on your lap, and have someone keep the patient's head between your hands in such a way that they are neither harmed nor agitated by holding their head.
Place a warm cloth soaked in oil or mullein juice on the eye of the patient.
Then apply the hot iron that is shaped like this:
which is concave, such as the shape of a reed or a feather quill, with one end from which the iron is made.
And if you wish, it should be penetrating into the other end. And if you want, let it come out in that way.
However, a concave one (thing) is better for the surgery.
Then press the fistula if it is opened, and draw out the pus and dry it up. If it is not opened, then open it and remove the pus from there.
And place your hand over the cautery, which should be well ignited, and hold the patient's nose with a small cloth at the edge of the nose to prevent your hand or the patient from being disturbed. Then press the cautery on the boil and burn it.
And if the cautery enters the bone at the beginning, it is good; otherwise, you should make another pass or two, as necessary. Leave it like that for three days, and then apply a bandage over the area with a dry dressing until it is healed.
However, if it has passed more than ten days and is not healed, then apply a sharp, corrosive medicine over it to expose the bone as necessary in its respective chapter.
And another method of cauterizing a fistula that some early authors mentioned: Press on the location of the fistula and open it, then place your hand in the resulting fissure as thinly as possible (the form of it), which should be about an inch of lead melted; hold your hand with good retention, and do not harm the patient so that the molten lead does not enter his nose. Cover the patient's nostril with alum of oil or water, because lead adheres to the location of the fistula and heals it by miraculous healing.
And if the fistula is healed with the method of cauterization and cure mentioned above, it is good; otherwise, it is necessary to administer trachea through the nose and reduce the fistula into the nose as it comes in its proper place.
Chapter XVIII.

Fifty-sixth Chapter

When a pain occurs in some limb by accident or injury, and the pain persists for a long time and does not respond to treatment with medications, then it is necessary to cauterize it using a pointed cautery.

But if pain with blood flow occurs, cauterize the affected area with a thin cautery (cauteril).
And the best cauterization is to make incisions and burn any remaining cause of the inflammation with fire; once they are cauterized with fire, the inflammation does not return.
Here comes the next sentence:
Treatment of swelling that affects the eyelids of some people.
Sometimes swelling that affects the eyelids of some people is accompanied by a cause similar in strength and durability to true swelling, and for this reason it is called "swelling."
And it is an accumulation of thick moisture on the upper and lower eyelids.
Therefore, the operation is to examine whether the swelling is coming from something that appears on the eyelid and is present everywhere; if this is the case, the cause is likely light.
Therefore make an incision along the width of it, then remove it from all sides with ease until it drains, and suspend it with a string and cut off the affected area.
And if the swelling is large, adjust it using stitches; care for it until it heals.
And if it is small, you will not suffer any harm from it, as the heat of the affected area restores and nourishes it.
If the swelling is gradually decreasing towards the inner parts of the eyelid, you should trim the affected area inside the eyelid, remove the swelling with a string, perform an incision if necessary, and press all around it; but if the eyelid is elongated due to repeated incisions, do not force it in any case.
After the incision, wash the wound with salt water; care for the affected area with something that nourishes it until it heals.
Here comes the next sentence:
Of the treatment applied to the upper eyelid of the eye.
Blinking is the action that is generated in the upper eyelid, especially among children, and worsens their eyesight and causes them to develop cataracts more; they cannot tolerate bright light due to tears forming at the eyes.
Therefore you often find them with tears constantly on their faces, even when they sleep; and the underside of their eyelids is moist, which is covered by inflammation, and the imminence of conjunctivitis is apparent in the eye; and whenever you press on the affected area with your fingers, you feel a swelling inside.
One method of operation is to have the patient hold their head between your knees, place a cloth and warm water on them, make a circle with it according to the size that contains arteries from all sides, and place it over the affected area and press around it so that swelling is created in the middle of the circle; then make an incision in the middle of the moisture along the width, but the incision should not be larger than the incision made during lithotomy.
But in the case of severe conjunctivitis, it is necessary that you cut the cordon completely through to the artery, as in more severe cases, conjunctivitis is treated by incision according to the shape of white pus.
Therefore you extract it with cloths that you have wrapped around your fingers at the front and sides, then turn it between your left and right hands until it is completely removed.
Keep watch that you do not press in the opening to prevent sputum from reaching the wound and causing contamination there.
If you do not enter the opening at first, but press into the opening to make a small space for sputum before processing it; and then extract that easily as we have said; submerge cloths in warm water and vinegar, place them on it and apply strong pressure with powders.
And mix salt and let it rest there in the depression of the incision to remove any remaining moisture.
Then care for that to ensure it heals.
If there is an abscess in the cauterized area, then care for it with caustic plasters until it heals.

Chapter .xiii.
On the cure of hernia that is made in the eyelid.
This hernia that is made in the eyelid, which is called truly hernia; and it is of a nature that is either natural or accidental.
Accidental is made by ulceration, cut, burning, or similar things.
The method of operation is that you take a needle with double thread and pierce it into the flesh, making it pass from the tear duct on the left to the tear duct on the right until the thread reaches both ends of the flesh.
Then stretch the skin at the edges with the needle and sew it up with the needle, and make an incision with a large spatula. And therefore if the figure of the eyelid returns as required, it is good; and if not, take the ray and place it in the slit figure, and with it convert the eyelid, and make two cuts along the edge of the left eyelid.
And the ends of both cuts are at two angles of the incision that you made until they meet, and form an angle between them until when they gather together the figure is formed.
And this figure is Greek letter L: lambda.
Then remove the skin in that amount equal to the length of the sharp part on the left side of the eyelid.
Then adjust the separated parts and sew them with wool thread, and heal them with what we have said about softening agents and ointments until they are healed.
And if hernia enters through a fissure or suture or burning, then it is necessary that you make an incision with a flat cut on the skin of the eyelid as previously mentioned. Then separate with ointment between the two lips as we have said.
In summary, the cure of hernia whether above or below, in operation, is prepared according to the form of hernia, and this is in the shape of various motes (lumps).
And the skillful craftsman always prepares tools for every method that is possible to return the figure to its natural form or as close as possible, and this patient according to what is necessary for the operation and tools in the best arrangement.
Chapter .xv.
On the adhesion of the eyelid to the conjunctiva or cornea.
When this consolidation occurs in many men who have the eyelid fused with the white part of the eye and is restricted in movement and its natural functions, therefore it is necessary that you insert the end of the finger below the eyelid, lift it up or stretch it with oil.
Then you cut the adhesion with a fine spatula, which is not sharp like an incision, having a blunt end so that the patient is not disturbed by the operation, and remove the spatula without damaging the eye with its sharpness.
And your incision should be as shallow as possible until the eyelid returns to its natural form and the entire adhesion is healed.
And place salt water in the eye and wash it with that, or distill in a vessel dissolved in water.
And separate the eyelid from the eye with ointment, and on the eye place wool soaked in egg yolk, and after three days use consolidating agents until it is healed.
Chapter .xvi.
On incision of nail and the prominence of skin of the tear ducts.
Know that the nail is of two types: either it is nerve-like and similar to hard dry substance; or it is not nerve-like, similar to frozen white moisture, which when touched by you or punctured, takes onion juice, is separated and the onion juice is not inserted in it.
And both types begin only from the major tear duct and gradually cover the eye, prevent light and movement of the eye.
But the method of working in the incision is that the patient rests his head on your shoulder, and you open his eyes, lift the eyelid with your hand, and collect the nail with onion juice and stretch it to the edges above. Then take a needle and insert it into the toe of an animal (such as horse, bull, cow, or similar), strong enough or double the tip of the needle little by little and place it in the middle of the nail, and penetrate with the needle through the nail, holding the nail; then pull it to the sides above, and peel off the skin from under the nail which contains the pupilla. And thus you follow the skin into the back of it.
Then you incise the remaining part of the nasal cavity with a sharp knife or small scissors, and open the natural nasal passage so that by incising it, continuous flow of tears is not caused.
Sometimes the nail with its root extended or thickened, as has been said, should be excised with lion-shaped spatula, which is the shape of it.
And be careful that with the spatula you do not touch the corneal tissue and cause rupture, and that the pupil is perforated.
Then make an incision in the nail with a little bit of powdered salt or vinegar and let it heal over the next day, and care for it until it heals.
And if the nail is not nervous and cannot be pierced with a needle or is not embedded in the root, it should be treated with this type of nail medicine, cured as described, and healed accordingly as recommended in the division.
And if you want to incise it, first open the patient's nail and take a fine lion-shaped spatula of sharp angle according to this form: with a sharp angle. And when it is rarefied and congealed and you find it blocked in the nail, then distill your oil of vinegar or rosewater or saltwater into the nail, and let it heal over the next day.
And apply the operation to it repeatedly until all that is in it has been removed, unless the counter-abscess has appeared on the nail, then you let it heal, and care for the abscess until it heals.
And repeat your operation on it with reason until it is healed.
The evacuation of the nasal cavity flesh, if noticed in the nail because of great harm, should be suspended with a nail; and incise it from one side, and do not extend the incision to prevent continuous flow of tears.
And apply rosewater or vinegar in the nasal cavity until it is healed.
Chapter XVII.
On the incision of a corn and what is born from flesh attached to the nail.
Sometimes in the nails of algae, red flesh is born and becomes inflamed until it covers the pupil or approaches or protrudes above the eyelids, and compresses the eyelids at the sides and resembles a rose bush with balustrade.

And your incision should be made with which you incise them or with the spatula that we have recommended in the nail incision, or with small scissors according to the form that will come according to this chapter.

If there remains any cause of algae and the wound becomes cauterized with blood, and you fear counter-abscess, let the nail heal and care for the abscess with what cures it, and apply the operation to it repeatedly until it is healed, similarly to the flesh that occurs in nails of this type.
However, you must be careful to avoid all healing of the nail naturally or accidentally, work with fire, and do not place your hand in any of these operations until you see that the member has suffered that operation.

Chapter XIX.
On reducing an arytenoid cartilage in the nose.
When you treat an arytenoid cartilage with cautery or sharp medicine as described earlier and it does not heal, do not be hasty but make a deep incision over the abscess to expose its maturity, and extract all the moisture that is in it and the pus, and let the bone be exposed.
And since the bone is exposed and you see corruption or blackness in it, then scrape it with an instrument of this shape:
It is called an instrument with a sharp head, and it should be made of iron, and the head should be round as if you were holding a ball that has been pierced by a small hole or alum pierced by a subtle hole (as shown in the following figure).
Place that instrument over the corrupt part of the bone, and gently rotate it between your fingers, and press your hand slowly until you know that the corruption has been scraped away.
Allow it to heal for some time, and then restore the area using drying and stiffening agents.
If the area is consolidated and good tissue grows over it, if the body rejects the sinus and remains for 40 days without being renewed or abscessed, and there is no accident in the area, then you will know that it has healed.
If not, then it is not in the ingenuity (skill or art), but to reduce the fissure to the shape of the nose, and as follows: and it is said that you discover according to how sharp your knife or medicine is, and when the bone is discovered, then you take three such:
Let the handle of the tool be triangular, and the shaft first be extended to the tip as often seen in such cases.
Place that one on the bone, and let that one be from the lacrimal (eye); then extend your thumb a little more, and press your hand against the three with your fingers inside until it penetrates all the bone, and let the patient feel it when it comes out.
Therefore, you restore the area with dry medicines that are astringent as they have been prescribed.
As the flesh and area hardens, you return the substance that flows from the wound to the nose, so it is easier for the patient.
Chapter 20.
On the reduction of the swelling on the thumb.
When the thumb swells completely without any harm or reduction, it is necessary to loosen the patient, and then to support him, and place poultices on his neck without scarification and use good sucking; and place liniment on the thumb which is made of aloes, opium, balm and saffron, and apply a plaster strongly on the thumb with lots of powder.
The method for powder is to take lions' hair cloth, and each piece should be folded four times; and make the powder from these.
And place one on top of the other according to the amount that the thumb requires. And apply strongly on these with hard cloth and tight bandage; and repeat the poultices without scarification and use good sucking; and remove the poultices and leave the thumb tied tightly for a day and a night.
But if during this time the ligament becomes softened, then it is necessary to be tightened more.
And remove the ligament after a day and a night as previously said.
If the thumb has already been reduced, that is good; but if not, then you repeat the plaster with powders and bandage and poultices until it heals.
Chapter 21.
On the incision of the swelling of the eyelid tunica (epithelium).
When there is a disruption in the eyelid tunica (epithelium) and it is swollen and protruding as if with a grain of sand, and its shape resembles that of man, and you wish to incise it, then the operation should be done as previously recommended, that you enter the needle into the wound from the lower part of the eyelid to the upper part, and place another needle at the lacrimal fold double line, and make it penetrate and release the first needle according to its position; and incise the location of the double thread and lift with it the wound edge in the circle of the needle, and tighten that area.
And extract the needle and place wool dipped in egg white on the wound, and press it until the thread comes out with the yolk.
And heal the wound with something that strengthens it until the wound is healed.
And add some bandages to all the sides of the wound in a circle around the swollen area, and perforate it with a thin spatula that touches the edge of the eyelid, let the white fluid (humid) run out, and press down on the swelling and enter immediately.
And tighten until it is healed.
Chapter 22.
On cauterization (burning).
This illness called "alconati" is not the same as the one that resembles water blisters, it is not that one.
But the method of working on it is that you make the patient sit on a stool covered with a cloth and upright, and take his head in your two hands from both sides and push him towards the wound so that the pus comes out from the bottom part, and let it dry and not descend, and let light come in, and let the patient see the causes as he saw before.
And if it does not descend (go down), you know that it is water.
But if the pus is not prepared to descend with what has been said, then make the patient sit between your hands and take a thin spatula and place it on the eyelid that surrounds a little the continuation of the conjunctiva and cornea in the crown (into the location used), until the pus is expelled.
Therefore, when it is expelled, you distill water (condense) in the wound which you have mixed with oil or water in which you have boiled fenugreek and honey.
And heal it with other causes until it is healed.
Chapter 23.
On the care of water coming out of the wound.
We have already said the species of water in the division and which one should be pierced with a serum as declared, then do that according to health.
Now you must tie the patient's hands together on a chair and bind their feet as well, pulling them tightly.
Then place your left hand near the patient's left eye (if it is the left eye with water), or your right hand if it is the right eye (if it is the right eye).
Then take the left-handed person's right hand (if it is the left eye), or the right-handed person's left hand (if it is the right eye).
Then place your left thumb near the corner of the eye (from the side with more water) for the swelling caused by the large vein in the eyelid of the smaller lacrimal duct, and apply pressure with your left hand on that spot.
Then make an incision in the eyelid (the area above the swollen part) and ensure that your thumb has reached it due to the swelling.
It is necessary to measure the distance from your thumb (almagda) to the eyebrow along the line of the eye, and that measurement is from the pupil to the end of the black part (corona), which you will see with the pupil's vision through the clarity of the cornea.
Place your thumb near the watery area (the eye with more water) and apply pressure on it several times until the water subsides. If the water goes down quickly, you will notice that the patient regains their sight in that eye.
Rest for a little while; if the water has subsided, then wait a bit more before releasing your thumb from that eye.
If the water does not subside, extract your thumb with ease and gently massage the eye several times, and then dissolve a small amount of clear salt in water and rinse the affected area with it; then stop or place warm compresses infused in rose oil and honey over the eye.

On the growths at the extremities of the nose.
These growths are called tela in the extremities of the nose, and they grow larger and become swollen on certain days before the regulation of the menses arrives.
Therefore, it is necessary to excise that at the beginning of its appearance, and to excavate all of it. Then place a compress or burning medicine on the site.

Chapter 30.
On the extraction of teeth.
You must treat the tooth pain thoroughly and patiently in its entire removal, for it is not a good reason to delay the healing of the wound when the tooth is removed, because there is a sublime substance entering that acts as an excuse during the extraction of the tooth.
But when the patient is ready to have that painful tooth removed, you must be certain of which tooth is causing the pain, for many a time the patient deceives himself and believes it is a healthy tooth, and you remove the wrong one, but the pain does not cease until the diseased and painful tooth is removed, as we have often seen in the practice of barbers.
Therefore, you must be certain of which tooth is causing the pain, and if you know this, then you should make an incision around the tooth with a spatula that has some virtue in it until the tooth is dissolved from the gum all around; then pull it out using forceps or fine forceps, gradually increasing the size until you have extracted it completely.
Bring some strong pliers with you, and hold the patient's head between large forceps that will speak well or have good structure, so that they do not move; and place the tooth in position according to correct procedure without breaking it or causing the patient any additional pain.
And thus, if you remember this, then take one of the instruments mentioned and remove the tooth easily and effortlessly as it was described at the beginning.
But if the tooth is broken or corroded, you must wrap it in cloth and tighten it at the root with a fine wire to prevent it from being crushed during your application of forceps.
You must work carefully with incisions around the entire gum and use great care to avoid breaking or splitting it further; then return to the patient, as the subsequent pain may be greater than the initial pain.
Be aware that you do not do what some ignorant barbers often do in their surgery and audacity during the removal of teeth, because they do not administer what we have recommended; for many times they bring upon men great ailments that are difficult to heal, and all or some of these remain, or that the tooth is extracted with bones from the jawbone as has happened many times.
And when removing the tooth, wash the mouth with water and salt to clean it.
And if bleeding occurs during this procedure, as has happened many times, take some wine and sprinkle it on the wound; if the wine does not stop the bleeding, cauterize it.
The shape of the forceps and fine forceps with which you will remove the tooth at the beginning should be long in length, short in width, and thick; this way they are not bent when working with them.
They should be as thick in the handles as necessary to avoid bending when gripping them, and have short lengths.
They should be made of steel from India and straight in shape, with teeth on the ends that grip each other tightly and exert strong pressure when closing; sometimes the ends of these forceps have the shape of a bird's beak called a ciconia, which has a strong grip.

"Here is the summary of the sermon on the opening and section on abscesses."
"Abscesses are many species, of many kinds, according to the memory of them in this book."
"They are diverse in perforation and section of them by two methods, one of which is for the species of abscesses that open themselves; and by the compression of humors."
"The second method is for the locations where accidents occur, because an abscess that occurs in the head is different from an abscess that occurs in the anus; and an abscess that occurs in a soft location is different from an abscess that occurs in a joint; and there is a treatment for each of them."
"However, some abscesses must not be perforated except for the maturation of pus or completion of them."
"Other abscesses must be drained when they are hard, and are not matured according to their completion, such as abscesses that occur near joints, because an abscess that occurs near a joint, the pain in it is prolonged until the surrounding area is purified and its ligaments or nerves of that joint are corrupted, causing contraction of that member; or an abscess that occurs in a major limb, if you delay the perforation of it until it has matured, it will spread to the main limb; or one that occurs near the anus, then do not drain the hard one without complete digestion, but the one that is proper to the anus, so that the anus does not expand and extend into the rectum and become a fistula, or that it is made at the edge of it which is not healed." You must know the time of the abscess's perforation, and that is when it has matured.
And you should know that it is matured when the pain subsides and the fever stops, and there is a decrease in swelling and pulse, and an increase in the sharpness of the abscess's head and other signs.
And you must know that the perforation should be made in the place below the abscess and where pus is flowing from the cure of the prominence.
The perforation should always be through the length of the flesh or the body, if the abscesses are in the groin or the legs, and in places of the ligaments, tendons, nerves, arteries; and finally, in all places where it is not reflected; because in those that are reflected, use perforation according to that member.
But when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to wait for its perforation until its digestion is confirmed according to the rules we have said; because if you perforate it before that, the course of the pus and motion is prolonged and the lips of it are hardened and the depth of it.
But some abscesses should be perforated according to the thickness of the flesh or the body depending on necessity, or according to what the member requires.
And you must administer a small perforation, and in large abscesses a large and wide or many small incisions according to the diversity of the size of the abscesses.

But that which is not like that, such as surface abscesses of lions, you must perforate with a superficial or flat perforation only.
And when the abscess is large and has collected pus, you must perforate it and do not hesitate to extract all the pus at that time; having extracted a part of it, you should return the abscess into it over another day, and you should extract a larger part, and make many pus observations according to gradation until it is forgotten.
In addition, if the patient is frail, or a woman in pregnancy, or a small child, or an old person in decrepitude, because animal spirit can often be resolved with the exit of pus, and strong liquor kills the patient, you should avoid these.
Be careful with this chapter and consider the quality of the wound when you perform the perforation on these abscesses; if the wound of the abscess is small, or it is a flat section, then you should administer some of it or old remedies; but if the abscess is large, and the fissures of the perforation are many, then you must pause every three hours until they come together.

But if it is in winter and the location of the abscess is near many nerves, then you must cover powders in wine and oil of caution, and pause those over the locations.
And if it is in summer and the locations are fleshy, then you must pause powders steeped in water and oil or in wine and oil, and all that should be warm until the third day as we have said, and then you must remove the abscess and avoid it and administer in its cure whatever is appropriate for it until it is healed.

Chapter xlv. (Chapter forty-fifth)
Of incision of the types of nodes.
The nodes have many different types, and I have already mentioned all their species in the division.
It is necessary to distinguish between a node and an abscess when there is doubt.
Therefore, I say that with an abscess there is heat, fever and strong pain until the boiling of the superfluidity subsides; it is a complete putrefaction which now stops the fever, the pain and the heat.
But with a node there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains that lion's head which is at the root.
And according to the color of the body, and it begins like a head and is made like an egg, whether large or small, and there are two types, either fatty with moisture, and the colors of the moisture are many, as I said in the division.
Therefore, when treating a node, it is necessary to expose it and investigate it at the beginning with a probe that is called intromes, according to its shape, as described in the relevant chapter.
And this is the method of investigation of abscesses and all nodes, and it is that you take this probe and insert it into the area with the most moisture where there is an abscess, and you turn your thumbs slowly into it until you know that the probe has penetrated the capsule.
Then place your hand on it according to the size of the abscess, and then extract the probe and consider what comes out from it as evidence.
If the moisture is discharged, no matter what its color, you should then incise it with a superficial incision as described in other abscesses.
If there is no moisture from the probe, you will know that it is fatty.
Dry over it with a cross-shaped incision in this manner: As you have learned, lift it up with the incision, peel off the capsule from all sides with ease, and keep the skin or sac if possible, over it and extract the pus with the node.
But if it is ruptured during the operation, it is not possible to extract the pus, and you should carefully watch for any discharge, and then extract it into pieces until no further cause remains.
Because if any cause remains, either a little or a lot, the node will return in the same manner.
And if you see that any small part remains, fill the wound with some sharp and corrosive powders and strengthen the wound, then place a cautery over it where there is an abscess, and care for the rest of it with other healing until it heals.
And if the node is large, you should then stitch the two lips of it and care for it with what is appropriate.
But if the pulsating vein is on the opposite side, or not pulsating, you should tie it and fill the area with vinegar that has been impregnated with lime (slaked lime) and hold it tightly for two to three days until the wound can be opened again and the bleeding stops; then return to incise what has been ruptured from the node.

Chapter .lii (51 in Roman numerals).
On the cure of protrusion of the navel.
Protrusion of the navel is caused by many reasons; either by fissures of the navel that are above the belly and from which the tissue or intestine emerges as in other ruptures; or by blood that flows from a vein or artery as previously mentioned, or by constricted ventilation in it.
But if it is due to a fissure of the navel and the exit of the tissue, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body; there is no pain, and it appears in various positions. If it is due to the exit of the intestine, then you should place its location in that area according to what has been recounted earlier, with much greater variation, and when you press it with your hands, it is hidden and returns; and strong pressure is required there, and it is greatly inflamed, so it must be introduced into hot water and vigorous work.
If it is due to moisture, then there is no pain and it is not hidden when pressed with the hand, nor is it constricted or swollen.
If it is due to blood, then you should use these signs to identify the abscess as darkening.
If it is flesh (affected), then it becomes a severe, large and hard abscess, and it is filled according to a certain quantity.
If it is windiness, then touch it with the lion (sponge soaked in vinegar or some other strong acid).
And the operation is that you consider whether the protrusion of the navel is due to blood from an artery, a vein or windiness; then it must be noted that you are forbidden to treat it, because in this case there is fear and dread, as I have taught you in the chapter about abscesses caused by an artery and a vein.
If the protrusion of the navel is due to the intestine or membrane, then you must command the patient to lie down on their back, and approach with a needle at the circumference of the entire navel, and command them to stay facing upwards between your hands, and surround the navel with a spatula in the circumference of the navel around the area that you have pointed out with the needle; then stretch out the abscess towards the armpits on one side and tie it with a strong thread or a cord, and use the appropriate method for tying it.
Then you cut the middle of the stretched-out abscess on the ligament and insert the needle there to pierce it, and if you have not found or protected it with the ligament, then you extract the pus and press the intestine towards the inside of the abdomen.
And if you have found the membrane, then take it with one hand; and cut away its excess.
But if it is opposed to your artery or vein, then surround that area and return to your operation; take two needles and insert them firmly into the circuit around the abscess in the manner of a cross, which you make penetrate; and then stretch out the abscess in four parts over the needles.
And if you wish, remove the needles and allow the stretched-out flesh to fall on its own; or cut where it is thin and can be pulled out, and then treat that with water until it heals.
If the protrusion of the navel is due to flesh or moisture, then you must compress the abscess as we have said and extract the blood or moisture, which you catch in it, and then treat that with water until it heals and consolidates the area.
Chapter 33.
On the treatment of ulcers.
We have already said in the division that there are various types of ulcers and what method is suitable for their treatment with medicines, and that it is inappropriate to treat them with iron because they will become ulcerated; and we have also mentioned that ulcers are formed due to carelessness and negligence in their treatment.
And the ancients said that in some cases ulcers can be eradicated in places where they can be excised, such as with an ulcer on the head or near the genitals and their equivalents on other parts of the body, especially when it starts small.
But when it becomes old and large, it is not necessary to treat it because it cannot be cured by anyone or I have not seen it being cured, nor has it been achieved.
The operation is as we have said, that you precede and wash the patient and purge them of black bile several times, and then cleanse that area if there is a clear repletion found.
Then prepare the patient with preparations suitable for surgery, and warn them about the dangers of the operation; then bend your knee deep into the abdomen until there is no remaining cause for the ulcer. Allow the blood to flow, do not open it lightly, and press on the areas, and remove all the thick blood with your hand or an instrument that you can handle among the available instruments.
But if it is difficult for you to cut thick blood in the vein or artery, then cauterize that area until the flow of blood stops and treat it with the appropriate treatment until it heals.
Chapter 40.
On the treatment of edema.
We have already recommended, in the division, the types of edema caused by water and the signs of each type, and their treatment with medicines.
And the type of edema that is cured with iron is only the one caused by altitude alone, and it should not be approached with iron for the types of edema of tympany or hypostasis, because that is deadly.
And when you have treated this type of edema caused by tympany with medicines and it does not improve, consider that if the patient is already weakened or has another type of edema such as in the throat or belly and similar, then do not treat them with iron because there is fear over it.
If you see the patient with excessive virtue (meaning strength or health), and it is not another illness but only edema, neither an infant nor an elderly person, then the method of operation on them is that you raise the patient between your hands, and provide them with a way to express their belly with their own hand, collect water at the junction below the navel, and take a sticky cotton swab in this manner:
It should be of two sharp points, long and pointed like a cotton swab; however, it should be in some small brevity, so that during the operation you do not pass into the intestine and cause damage to it.
Then consider if the edema generation is from the intestines, for then you must be away from the navel by about three fingers below, on its right side near the navel.
But if the edema generation is due to kidney disease, then your incision should be on its left side from the navel by about three fingers.
And if it is due to the liver, then your incision should be on its right side.
And it is necessary that your incision is over the ribs where the patient wants to lie, so that the exudations do not flow towards that location.

Chapter LXIX.
On castration.
Know that castration in our law is forbidden, but it is appropriate to remind me of it in this book; and the reminder is necessary only in two cases, one of which is when the physician is asked about it because he knows the cure for such [conditions], and the other case is when we have a need for castration of other animals for our benefit as with horses, cows, pigs, etc., and similar animals.
And thus it is said that castration is done in two ways: either by strangulation, or by incision.
But in the method done by strangulation, the procedure is that we strangle the animal in warm water until its testicles become softened and hang down. Then take those [testicles] with your hand until they are resolved and do not appear again.
But in castration done by incision and section, it is necessary that you hold the animal and press the scrotum of [the testicles] with your left hand.
Then pull back the scrotal sac, and incise each tube with one section until two tubes are exposed.

The treatment is of three types: one for men and one type for women. It is necessary that you incise the flesh and adjust it so that the pain of [the hermaphrodite] subsides, and then treat it with care for other sores.
